EXPLANATORY STATEMENT

This Bill seeks to consolidate the Securities Industry Act 1983 ("Act 280") and the
Futures Industry Act 1993 ("Act 499"), and the relevant provisions in relation to
fund raising activities under the Securities Commission Act 1993 ("Act 498"), and
to provide for matters incidental thereto and connected therewith.

The scope of the proposed Act is as follows:

-  to introduce a single licensing framework for capital market
intermediaries;

-  to promote Malaysia as a global Islamic financial hub;

-  to modernise the regulatory framework in relation to financial markets and
products;

-  to streamline fund raising activities and strengthen the protection of
investors; and

-  to provide for the establishment and the supervisory framework for selfregulatory organizations in the capital market.

2. _Clause 1_ contains the short title and the power of the Minister to appoint

different commencement dates for different provisions of this proposed Act.

3. _Clause 2 seeks to define certain words and expressions used in the proposed_

Act. Some of the salient definitions are as follows:

the definition of "approved clearing house" which shall be an approved clearing

house in place of an approved clearing house under Act 499 and a recognized
clearing house under Act 280.

the definitions of "Capital Markets Services Licence", "Capital Markets Services

Representative's Licence" and "regulated activity" have been introduced in order to
give effect to the single licensing framework which is one of the main thrusts of the
proposed Act. "Regulated activities" for the purposes of the proposed Act is further
described in Schedule 2.

the definition of "self-regulatory organization" incorporates a framework that

provides for the recognition and oversight of a recognized self-regulatory
organization.

4. _Clause 3_ deals with the term "associated person". It seeks to set out a list

of persons who shall be deemed as persons associated with another person.


-----

446 _Bill_

_5._ _Clause 4 deals with the term "interest in securities". It seeks to set out a list of_

what constitutes interest in securities.

6. _Clause 5_ seeks to provide for the prescription of securities and futures

contracts.

7. _Clause 6_ seeks to provide for the consequences of agreements becoming a

futures contract.

8. _Clause 7_ seeks to provide for the establishment of stock market, futures

market, exempt stock market and exempt futures market. This _clause_ also
introduces a new category of markets known as "registered electronic facility".

9. _Clause 8_ seeks to provide for the power of the Minister to approve a stock

exchange and a futures exchange.

10. _Clause 9_ seeks to provide for the power of the Commission to approve any
amendments made to the rules of the stock exchange, the futures exchange and an
approved clearing house.

11. _Clause 10_ seeks to establish a public interest framework in relation to the
composition of the board of directors of an exchange holding company, a stock
exchange and a futures exchange. This _clause_ provides that the boards of these
market institutions must comprise of a specified number of public interest directors
that are to be appointed by the Minister.

12. _Clause 11_ seeks to provide for the duties of the stock exchange and futures
exchange.

13. _Clause 12_ empowers the Minister to withdraw an approval given to a stock
exchange or futures exchange pursuant to clause 8. The effect of the withdrawal of
such approval is provided for in clause 13.

14. _Clause 14_ seeks to provide that an exchange holding company or a holding
company of an exchange holding company may only be established with the
approval of the Minister. The approval process that must be complied with in order
to establish an exchange holding company is provided for in clause 15.

15. _Clause 16_ requires a stock exchange, a futures exchange and an exchange
holding company to submit to the Commission an annual regulatory report.

16. _Clause 17_ empowers the Minister to require a stock exchange, a futures
exchange or an exchange holding company to prepare and submit to him at any
time a special report on their compliance with the requirements of the proposed
Act, and any provisions of the securities laws and rules.

17. _Clause 18_ empowers the Minister to withdraw an approval given to an
exchange holding company. The effect of such withdrawal is provided in clause 19.


-----

_Capital Markets and Services_ 447

18. _Clause 20 seeks to provide for the listing of the exchange holding company on_
the stock exchange.

19. _Clause 21 seeks to set out the various duties of an exchange holding company._

20. _Clause 22 imposes the requirement of having to establish a Risk Management_
Committee on an exchange holding company.

21. _Clause 23_ imposes restrictions on an exchange holding company from
reducing its shareholdings in its subsidiaries.

22. _Clause 24 seeks to require an exchange holding company, a stock exchange, a_
futures exchange, an approved clearing house, a central depository and any other
relevant body corporate to notify the Commission of its intention to dispose or
acquire assets that may have been specified by the Commission.

23. _Clause 25_ imposes restriction on acquiring a substantial shareholding in an
exchange holding company.

24. _Clause 26_ empowers the Commission to issue directions to the exchange
holding company, stock exchange, futures exchange, approved clearing house,
central depository and any other relevant body corporate to deal with matters of
conflict of interest.

25. _Clause 27 provides for the procedure for the closure of the stock exchange or_
futures exchange in the case of an emergency.

26. _Clause 28_ empowers the Commission to prohibit trading on the stock
exchange or futures exchange.

27. _Clause 29 requires an exchange holding company, a stock exchange, a futures_
exchange and an approved clearing house to provide such assistance to the
Commission as it may reasonably require.

28. _Clause 30_ seeks to enable the Minister to issue suspension orders on an.
exchange holding company, a stock exchange, a futures exchange, an approved
clearing house or a central depository for the purpose of protecting investors.

29. _Clause 31_ seeks to set out the various actions that the Commission can take
upon contravention of clause 23, 24 or 25 of the proposed Act.

30. _Clause 32_ empowers the Commission to publish a notice in relation to any
action taken by the Minister or the Commission under clause 12, 18, 27, 354 or 355
of the proposed Act.

31. _Clause 33_ seeks to provide that the rights of a stock exchange, a futures
exchange, an approved clearing house or parties to a futures contract shall not be
affected by any written laws relating to a contract.


-----

448 _Bill_

32. _Clause 34_ seeks to introduce a new provision to enable the Commission to
register an electronic facility, This provision also enables the Commission to
impose terms and conditions on the operator of the electronic facility to ensure that
an orderly and fair market exists in relation to transactions that are carried out
through the registered electronic facility. The registration process for the electronic
facility is provided for in clause 35.

33. _Clause 36 empowers the Commission to withdraw the registered status that has_
been accorded to an electronic facility and that the Commission may do so if,
among others, it is in the interest of investors or for the maintenance of an orderly
and fair market.

34. _Clause 37_ seeks to prohibit the provision of unauthorised clearing facilities.
Unauthorised clearing facilities refers to clearing facilities that have not been
approved by the Commission.

35. _Clause 38_ seeks to provide for the approval process that must be complied
with in order to provide clearing house facilities. This _clause_ enables the
Commission, with the concurrence of the Minister, to approve a clearing house.
The withdrawal of an approval accorded to an approved clearing house is provided
for in clause 39. The effect of withdrawal of an approval is specified in clause 40.

36. _Clauses 41 to 57 seek to modify the law of insolvency and other miscellaneous_
provisions relating to the operations and procedures of an approved clearing house.

37. _Clause 58_ seeks to require a capital market intermediary to hold a Capital
Markets Services Licence in order to carry on a business in any of the regulated
activities specified in Schedule 2 of the proposed Act. This _clause_ seeks to give
effect to the single licensing regime. Hence, intermediaries will only require one
licence to carry on activities in the securities and futures industry. This clause also
provides that specified persons listed out in Schedule 3 do not need to hold a
Capital Markets Services Licence.

38. _Clause 59 seeks to require a representative of a capital market intermediary to_
also hold a Capital Markets Services Representative's Licence.

39. _Clause 60_ seeks to provide for the application procedure for the grant or
renewal of a Capital Markets Services Licence and Capital Markets Services
Representative's Licence.

40. _Clause 61_ empowers the Commission to grant or renew a Capital Markets
Services Licence or Capital Markets Services Representative's Licence. In the case
of granting or renewing a Capital Markets Services Licence for carrying on a
business of dealing in securities or trading in futures contracts, the clause provides
that the Commission, with the concurrence of the Minister, may grant or renew
such a licence.

41. _Clause 62_ empowers the Commission to impose conditions or restrictions
on the licences that the Commission issues provided that in the case of a
Capital Markets Services Licence for carrying on a business of dealing in


-----

_Capital Markets and Services_ 449

securities or trading in futures contracts, conditions can only be imposed with the
concurrence of the Minister.

42. _Clause 63 seeks to provide for the payment of a prescribed licence fee and that_
the licence fee collected by the Commission shall be paid into the Federal
Consolidated Fund.

43. _Clause 64_ seeks to provide a transparent criteria in assessing whether an
applicant for a Capital Markets Services Licence is fit and proper. Clause 65 on the
other hand specifies fit and proper criteria in relation to an applicant for a Capital
Markets Services Representative's Licence.

44. _Clause 66 empowers the Commission to enquire into transactions in respect of_
securities and futures contracts.

45. _Clause 67 seeks to provide that holders of a Capital Markets Services Licence_
shall meet the minimum financial requirements as specified by the Commission
before it can carry on any regulated activity.

46. _Clause 68 spells out the duration of a licence._

47. _Clause 69_ empowers the Commission to vary a Capital Markets Services
Licence or Capital Markets Services Representative's Licence.

48. _Clause 70 requires a holder of a Capital Markets Services Licence carrying on_
a business of dealing in securities (other than participating organization) or fund
management to lodge a deposit of RM 150,000 with the Commission or such other
amount as the Minister may prescribe or take up insurance for the indemnification
of claims up to an amount of RM 150,000 or such other amount, as the Minister
may prescribe.

49. _Clause 71_ prohibits the making of false statements in relation to the
application for the grant, renewal or variation of the Capital Markets Services
Licence or Capital Markets Services Representative's Licence.

50. _Clause 72 empowers the Commission to revoke or suspend a Capital Markets_
Services Licence or Capital Markets Services Representative's Licence. The effect
of revocation, suspension or expiry of a Capital Markets Services Licence is
provided for in clause 73.

51. _Clause 74_ requires a licensed person to notify the Commission of any
disqualifying event.

52. _Clause 75 introduces a new provision to enable a holder of a Capital Markets_
Services Licence to appoint its directors and chief executive and to notify the
Commission of the appointment, election and nomination of such persons.
Responsibility is placed on the licence holder as well as on the individual who is to
be appointed as a director or chief executive to ensure that he is fit and proper. In
the event the person appointed as a director or chief executive is not fit and proper
and continues to hold office, the Commission may issue a direction to the licence
holder to remove that director or chief executive.


-----

450 _Bill_

53. _Clause 76_ introduces a new category of intermediaries who are allowed to
carry on capital market activities without having to hold a Capital Markets Services
Licence. These persons are referred to as "registered persons" and includes persons
and institutions that are specified in Schedule 4.

54. _Clause 77_ empowers the Commission to establish and maintain a register of
holders of a Capital Markets Services Licence and Capital Markets Services
Representative's Licence.

55. _Clause 78 requires a holder of a Capital Markets Services Licence or Capital_
Markets Services Representative's Licence to notify the Commission of any change
in material particulars.

56. _Clause 79 enables the Commission to publish the names and addresses of all_
licence persons.

57. _Clause 80_ provides that an appeal can be made to the Minister against the
decision of the Commission in its refusal to grant, revoke or suspend a Capital
Markets Services Licence.

58. _Clause 81_ sets out the process for surrendering the Capital Markets Services
Licence or Capital Markets Services Representative's Licence to the Commission.

59. _Clause 82 sets out the persons to whom Division 2 of Part III of the proposed_
Act shall apply which includes a licensed person who carries on the business of
either dealing in securities, fund management, advising on corporate finance,
investment advice or financial planning, financial journalist and an authorised
depository agent. In clause 83, such persons shall establish and maintain a register
of securities whereby particulars of the securities in which the specified person has
an interest in must be entered into the register. Such persons shall notify the
Commission of the place at which the register of securities is maintained as
provided for in clause 84.

60. _Clause 85_ seeks to provide for a defence to prosecution in relation to cases
involving a contravention of clause 83 or 84 of the proposed Act.

61. _Clause 86 deals with of the requirement to produce the register of securities for_
inspection purposes.

62. _Clause 87_ enables the Commission to require certain persons to supply the
Commission with particulars of financial journalist.

63. _Clause 88_ enables the Commission to supply a copy of the extract of the
register of securities to any person on payment of a specified fee.

64. _Clause 89 prohibits against the making of certain representations by a licensed_
person.

65. _Clause 90_ empowers the Minister to make regulations in relation to the
issuance of contract notes.


-----

_Capital Markets and Services_ 451

66. _Clause 91_ requires a licensed person to disclose its interest in any securities
that it has recommended.

67. _Clause 92 requires a licensed person to have a reasonable basis for providing_
advise or making recommendation to a client.

68. _Clause 93 requires a licensed person who carries on the business of dealing in_
securities or fund management to give priority to its client order.

69. _Clause 94 seeks to set out a restriction on dealings in securities by employees_
of a holder of a Capital Markets Services Licence or of a participating
organization.

70. _Clause 95 requires a holder of a Capital Markets Services Licence to submit to_
the Commission returns and any information relating to its business as may be
required by the Commission.

71. _Clause 96_ empowers the Commission to impose additional obligations on a
licensed person.

72. _Clause 97 provides for the prohibition against dealing as a principal on holders_
of a Capital Markets Services Licence who carries on the business of dealing in
securities.

73. _Clause 98 provides for the general prohibition against shortselling as well as_
the situations in which the prohibition would not apply.

74. _Clause 99 requires a holder of a Capital Markets Services Licence who carries_
on the business of trading in futures contracts to not knowingly take the other side
of an order of a client unless the client has consented to the taking of that order.

75. _Clause 100_ requires a holder of a Capital Markets Services Licence who
carries on the business of trading in futures contracts or fund management in
respect of futures contracts to provide its prospective client with a risk disclosure
document or any other information as may be specified by the Commission.

76. _Clause 101_ empowers the Commission to fix positions and trading limits in
futures contracts.

77. _Clause 102 empowers the Commission to fix or vary the reportable positioning_
in relation to futures contracts.

78. _Clause 103 specifically provides that a futures contract shall not be taken to be_
a gaming or wagering contract.

79. _Clause 104 sets out the requirement for the sequencing of sending and carrying_
out of orders in respect of trading in futures contracts.

80. _Clause 105_ provides for a general prohibition against trading in futures
contracts on a futures market that is outside Malaysia unless trading is on a


-----

452 _Bill_

futures market of a specified exchange or trading is in respect of an approved class
of futures contracts. This clause allows the futures exchange to specify exchanges
and to approve the class of futures contracts.

81. _Clause 106_ provides for the requirement that in order to carry on trading in
futures contracts on a specified exchange, such holders would have to pay to the
Commission a specified amount that would be applied to deal with prescribed
events such as the insolvency of the holder.

82. _Clause 107 imposes criminal liability on persons who contravene clauses 99,_
_100, 101, 102 and 104 of the proposed Act._

83. _Clause 108_ requires a holder of a Capital Markets Services Licence to
maintain such records that can explain the transactions and financial position of its
business.

84. _Clauses 109 and 110 provide that the application of Subdivision 2 of Division_
4 of Part III of the proposed Act is confined to a holder of a Capital Markets
Services Licence who carries on the business of dealing in securities and defines
terms such as "client assets" for the purposes of the Subdivision.

85. _Clause 111_ requires a holder of a Capital Markets Services Licence who
carries on the business of dealing in securities to place monies received into a trust
account.

86. _Clause 112_ specifies how client's assets received (other than in the form of
monies received) by a holder of a Capital Markets Services Licence who carries on
the business of dealing in securities are to be dealt with.

87. _Clause 113 sets out the circumstances in which a holder of a Capital Markets_
Services Licence who carries on the business of dealing in securities may withdraw
monies from a trust account.

88. _Clause 114_ requires a holder of a Capital Markets Services Licence who
carries on the business of dealing in securities to supply copies of entries in its
books when requested by its client.

89. _Clause 115_ deals with the protection provided for monies held in a trust
account against other claims or liens.

90. _Clauses 116 and 117 provide that the application of Subdivision 3 of Division_
4 of Part III of the proposed Act is confined to a holder of a Capital Markets
Services Licence who carries on the business of trading in futures contracts and
define terms such as "client assets", "property" and "client" for the purposes of the
Subdivision.

91. _Clause 118 provides that a holder of a Capital Markets Services Licence who_
carries on the business of trading in futures contracts must maintain a client's
segregated account for monies and assets received from its client. Clause 119 states
that monies or assets in the client's segregated account shall not be used to pay off
any debt or liability of the holder of the Licence.


-----

_Capital Markets and Services_ 453

92. _Clauses 120 and 121 provide that the application of Subdivision 4 of Division_
4 of Part III of the proposed Act is confined to a holder of a Capital Markets
Services Licence who carries on the business of fund management and defines
terms such as "trust account", "client's assets" and "custodian" for the purposes of
the Subdivision.

93. _Clause 122_ requires a holder of a Capital Markets Services Licence who
carries on the business of fund management to appoint a custodian that will
maintain a trust account. Client's monies and assets received by such holder shall
be paid or deposited into the trust account.

94. _Clause 123_ specifies how client's assets received by a holder of a Capital
Markets Services Licence who carries on the business of fund management are to
be dealt with.

95. _Clause 124_ requires a holder of a Capital Markets Services Licence who
carries on the business of fund management to supply its client with copies of
entries in his book relating to the client's transaction.

96. _Clause 125_ sets out actions that may be taken by the Commission for the
purpose of protecting client's assets or client's interest when the licensed person or
an approved trustee has contravened the proposed Act or any guidelines.

97. _Clause 126 spells out the requirement for the appointment of auditors and the_
prohibition against the appointment of associates as auditors by relevant persons.
The provision further specifies that relevant persons are holders of a Capital
Markets Services Licence, an exchange holding company, a stock exchange, a
futures exchange, an approved clearing house, a central depository and a recognised
self-regulatory organization. In _clause 127,_ the relevant person shall lodge an
auditor's report with the Commission within three months of the close of each
financial year or such further period as may be specified by the Commission.

98. _Clause 128_ sets out the duties of the auditors to report to the Commission,

the stock exchange or the futures exchange, as the case may be, of any breach of
the proposed Act, the securities laws or any irregularity that may have a material
effect on the accounts of the relevant person.

99. _Clause 129_ requires a relevant person or any of its directors to provide the

auditors with relevant information.

100. _Clause 130 empowers the Commission to appoint independent auditors in the_
event the relevant person has failed to lodge an auditor's report with the
Commission as required by _clause 127_ or where the Commission has received a
report under clause 127 or 128.

101. _Clause 131_ empowers the Commission to appoint an independent auditor
upon the application of a client of a relevant person.

102. _Clause 132_ requires an independent auditor who is appointed by the
Commission under _clause 130_ or _131_ to report to the Commission his findings
upon the conclusion of his examination.


-----

454 _Bill_

103. _Clause 133 provides for the powers of an independent auditor appointed by_
the Commission. The powers include examination of persons and employing such
persons as may be necessary to carry out the examination for which the
independent auditor was appointed for.

104. _Clause 134_ prohibits independent auditors from communicating certain
matters to any persons other than the Commission.

105. _Clause 135_ deals with the powers of an independent auditor to request for
books, accounts and records of a relevant person.

106. _Clause 136 sets out the penalty for destroying, concealing or altering books._

107. _Clause 137 spells out the right of a stock exchange or a futures exchange to_
impose further obligations on a participating organization or a holder of a Capital
Markets Services Licence who carries on the business of trading in futures
contracts in relation to audit of accounts.

108. _Clauses 138 and 139 seek to facilitate the transfer of business by one licence_
holder to another by way of a vesting order from the court.

109. _Clauses 140 to 158 provide for the establishment, contribution, maintenance_
and application of the compensation fund by a stock exchange. The compensation
fund is to be applied to compensate persons who have suffered monetary loss as a
result of the insolvency of the participating organization or as a result of any
defalcation or fraudulent misuse of monies or other property by a director, officer,
employee or representative of a holder of a Capital Markets Services Licence who
carries the business of dealing in securities and who is also a participating
organization of the stock exchange.

110. _Clauses 159 to 173 provide for the establishment, contribution, maintenance_
and application of the fidelity fund by a futures exchange. The fidelity fund is to be
applied to compensate persons who have suffered monetary loss as a result of any
defalcation or fraudulent misuse of monies or other property by a director, officer,
employee or representative of a holder of a Capital Markets Services Licence who
carries on the business of trading in futures contracts and who is an affiliate of the
futures exchange.

111. _Clause 174_ deals with the application of Divisions 1 and 2 of Part V.
Division 1 sets out the various market offences in respect of the securities while
Division 2 sets out the various market offences in respect of futures contract.

112. _Clauses 175, 176 and 777 deal with the prohibition against false trading and_
market rigging transactions, stock market manipulations and the making of false
and misleading statements respectively.

113. _Clauses 178_ and _179_ set out the prohibition against fraudulently inducing
persons to deal in securities and the use of manipulative and deceptive devices in
connection with the subscription, purchase or sale of securities respectively.


-----

_Capital Markets and Services_ 455

114. _Clause 180_ empowers the Minister to prescribe and make regulations to
exempt any persons from the application of clause 175 or 776.

115. _Clause 181_ prohibits the dissemination of information about illegal
transactions.

116. _Clause 182_ provides for the penalty for offences committed against _clause_
_175, 176, 177, 178, 179 or 181._

117. _Clauses 183_ to _198_ deal with the prohibition against insider trading. The
_clauses define various terms that are relevant for the offence of insider trading and_
the defences that are available.

118. _Clause 199_ sets out the civil liability for the contravention of _clause 175,_
_176, 177, 178, 179 or 181. It provides that any person who suffers loss or damage_
as a result of the conduct of another person who has contravened any of the
provisions may recover that loss or damage by instituting civil proceedings against
that other person.

119. _Clause 200_ provides for civil proceedings for the contravention of _clause_
_175, 176, 177, 178, 179 or 181. It provides that the Commission may institute civil_
proceedings against a person who has contravened any of the provisions although
that person may not have been charged with an offence. The Commission may
recover an amount which shall not exceed three times the gross amount of
pecuniary gain made or loss avoided by the person in breach. It also allows the
Commission to claim a civil penalty against the person in breach for an amount not
exceeding one million ringgit.

120. _Clause 201_ enables any person who suffer losses or damages as a result of
the conduct of another person who has contravened clause 188 to recover that loss
or damages by instituting civil proceedings against that person.

121. _Clauses 202_ to _209_ set out the various market offences in relation to the
futures contract. These clauses respectively provide for the offence of false trading,
bucketing, manipulation of price of futures contract, employment of devices to
defraud and making a false or misleading statement to induce another to enter into
a futures contract.

122. _Clause 210 deals with civil liability for the contravention of clause 202, 203,_
_204, 205, 206, 207 or 208 It provides that any person who suffers loss or damage as_
a result of the conduct of another person who has contravened any of the said
provisions may recover that loss or damage by instituting civil proceedings against
that person.

123. _Clause 211_ provides for civil proceedings for the contravention of _clauses_
_202, 203, 204, 205, 206, 207 or 208. It provides that the Commission may institute_
civil proceedings against a person who has contravened any of the said provisions
although that person may not be charged with an offence. This clause provides that
the Commission may recover an amount which shall not exceed three times the
gross amount of pecuniary gain made or loss avoided by the person in breach. It
also allows the Commission to claim a civil penalty against the person for an
amount not exceeding one million ringgit.


-----

456 _Bill_

124. _Clauses 212_ to _316_ relate to the fund raising provisions which have been
transferred from Part IV of the Act 498. This inclusion would ensure that the
substantive provisions regulating the securities and futures industry are provided
for in the proposed Act.

125. _Clause_ 317 deals with the chief executive and directors of a listed
corporation who have an interest in the securities of the listed corporation shall
notify the listed corporation in writing of his interest and extent of his interest in
the securities unless exempted by the Commission.

126. _Clause 318 provides for the disqualification of an unfit person to be the chief_
executive or director of a listed corporation.

127. _Clause 319 requires a listed corporation to submit to the Commission a copy_
of its audited annual accounts and its interim and periodic financial reports.

128. _Clause 320 provides for the duties of an auditor of a listed corporation._

129. _Clause 321 provides for the protection of persons against any retaliation for_
reporting to the Commission or to the stock exchange of any breach or nonperformance of any requirement or provisions of the proposed Act or securities
laws or any rules of the stock exchange.

130. _Clause 322_ defines the term "chief executive", "director" and "officer" in
respect of a self-regulatory organization.

131. _Clause 323 provides for the power of the Commission, with the concurrence_
of the Minister, to recognize a self-regulatory organization. This _clause_ also sets
out the minimum conditions that must be satisfied before a self-regulatory
organization can be accorded with recognised status.

132. _Clause_ 324 provides for the duties of a recognized self-regulatory
organization while _clause_ 325 provides that such organization cannot amend its
rules without prior approval of the Commission.

133. _Clause_ 326 states that a recognized self-regulatory organization shall not
appoint a person as its chief executive or director without prior approval of the
Commission.

134. _Clause_ 327 confers on the Commission the power to issue directions to a
recognized self-regulatory organization when there is a conflict between the
interest of the organization and its duties under the proposed Act.

135. _Clause_ 328 confers on the Commission the power, with the concurrence of
the Minister, to withdraw the recognized status that has been accorded on to a selfregulatory organization.

136. _Clause 329 states that a recognized self-regulatory organization, its officers_
and employees will not be liable for anything done or omitted to be done in the
performance of their duties or functions as a recognized self-regulatory
organization.


-----

_Capital Markets and Services_ 457

137. _Clause_ 330 provides that the audit of a recognized self-regulatory
organization shall be carried out in accordance to the provisions of Subdivision 6
of Division 4 of Part III of the proposed Act.

138. _Clauses 332_ to _346_ deal with the provisions relating to the Capital Market
Development Fund. These _clauses_ seek to provide for the establishment, objects
and administration of the Capital Market Development Fund. The Fund shall be
administered by the Capital Market Development Fund Board whose members
shall be appointed by the Minister.

139. _Clause 347 deals with the application of Part X of the proposed Act which_
provides for the disclosure of information to the Commission in order to enable the
Commission to enforce the provisions of the proposed Act. Its provisions,
however, do not extend to licensed institutions and Islamic banks but would apply
to a licensed institution that holds a Capital Markets Services Licence.

140. _Clause 348 confers on the Commission the power to require the production_
of books. The penalty for the contravention of the requirement mentioned in clause
_348 is provided for in clause 349._

141. _Clause 350_ empowers the Commission to specify the form and manner in
which the information, returns or documents are required to be submitted to the
Commission and the period for that submission.

142. _Clause 351 sets out the protection provided for an advocate and solicitor in_
relation to privileged information.

143. _Clause 352_ confers the power to the Commission to require a holder of a
Capital Market Services Licence who carries on the business of dealing in
securities or trading in futures contracts to disclose to the Commission specified
information in relation to such dealing or trading.

144. _Clause 353 provides for the power of the Commission to require any person_
to disclose to the Commission information relating to dealing in securities or
trading in futures contracts.

145. _Clauses 354_ and _355_ confer the power to the Commission to take various
administrative actions against persons that are specified in those clauses.

146. _Clause 356 provides for the power of the Commission to take administrative_
actions against a licensed person for contravening or failing to comply with any
requirement, or provision of any securities laws, written notice, guidelines or
conditions or restrictions imposed on the licence granted to the licensed person.

147. _Clause 357 sets out the civil liability for the contravention of Part VI of the_
proposed Act. It provides that any person who suffers loss or damage as a result of
the conduct of another person who has contravened any of the


-----

458 _Bill_

provisions of Part VI or any regulations made under the proposed Act, may recover
that loss or damage by instituting civil proceeding against that person. Clause 358
relates to the power of the Commission to recover loss or damage on behalf of
other persons who have suffered loss by the conduct of another person who has
contravened that Part.

148. _Clause 359 clarifies the reference to conduct in relation to the activities under_
Part VI of the proposed Act.

149. _Clause 360_ empowers the court to make certain orders if applied for by,
among others, the Commission, the exchange holding company, a stock exchange,
a futures exchange and an approved clearing house.

150. _Clause 361_ provides the authority to the Commission, a stock exchange, a
futures exchange or an approved clearing house to apply to the court to wind up a
company under specified grounds.

151. _Clause 362_ prohibits the use of certain titles such as "participating
organization", "exchange holding company", "futures exchange", _etc._ It also
prohibits a non-licensed person from using a title or description implying that the
person is a licensed person.

152. _Clause 363 relates to evidence obtained from a copy of the book maintained_
by a stock exchange, a futures exchange or a holder of a Capital Markets Services
Licence.

153. _Clause 364_ provides a means for an aggrieved party to apply to the
Commission to have the Commission review its own decisions made pursuant to
the proposed Act. Clause 365 provides for the time that the application referred to
in clause 364 must be made.

154. _Clause 366_ provides that any decision made by the Minister under the
proposed Act shall be final.

155. _Clause 367_ clarifies the relationship between a body corporate and its
officers in relation to offences.

156. _Clause 368_ prohibits the falsification of records while _clause 369_ prohibits
the making and submission of any false report to the Commission, stock exchange,
futures exchange or an approved clearing house.

157. _Clause 370 deals with a provision for attempts, abetments and conspiracies in_
relation to offences under the proposed Act.

158. _Clause 371_ prohibits against the destruction, concealment, mutilation and
alteration of records by any person.

159. _Clause 372 provides for a general penalty for the proposed Act._

160. _Clause 373_ provides that the Commission, with the consent of the Public
Prosecutor, may compound any offence committed by a person against Part II, HI,
VI, VII, X or XII of the proposed Act, or any regulations made thereunder.


-----

_Capital Markets and Services_ 459

161. _Clause 374_ requires persons convicted under Part V or VI of the proposed
Act to pay compensation as may be determined by the court to any person who has
suffered loss or damage as a result of the offence committed by the convicted
person.

162. _Clause 375_ specifically states that no prosecution for an offence under the
proposed Act may be instituted without a written consent from the Public
Prosecutor.

163. _Clause 376_ provides that no civil liability shall be incurred by a stock
exchange, a futures exchange, an exchange holding company, an approved clearing
house or a central depository and by its officers for anything done, or any statement
made in connection with the discharge of any of its duties under the proposed Act,
the securities laws or its rules.

164. _Clause 377_ empowers the Commission to issue guidelines and practice
notes.

165. _Clause 378_ provides for the power of the Minister to make regulations. It
also provides that the Minister may make regulations pertaining to matters
specified in Schedule 10 of the proposed Act.

166. _Clause 379 provides that the rules of a stock exchange, a futures exchange, a_
central depository or an approved clearing house may make provisions for the
settlement of disputes. The _clause_ also provides that the Minister can make
regulations for the settlement of disputes.

167. _Clause 380 provides for the power of the Minister to amend the Schedules to_
the proposed Act.

168. _Clause 381 provides for the repeal of Act 280 and Act 499, saving provision_
of any regulations, directions, notifications, exemptions, orders, approvals,
decisions, applications and transactions that were issued or entered into under both
the repealed Acts.

169. _Clause 382 saves the approvals granted to the various market institutions that_
have been approved or recognised under the repealed Act 280 and Act 499 and
preserves any conditions or restrictions that have been imposed by the Minister
when approving or recognising these institutions.

170. _Clause 383_ states that the electronic broking system which was accorded
exempt stock market status under the Securities Industry (Declaration of Exempt
Stock Market) Order 2005 shall be deemed to be a registered electronic facility for
the purposes of the proposed Act.

171. _Clauses 384_ and _385_ respectively relate to the preservation of the various
intermediary licences that have been issued under the repealed Acts 280 and Act
499 and the applications made for intermediary licences under both Acts.

172. _Clause 386 deals with saving provisions relating to rules, orders, approvals,_
decisions and regulations issued or made pursuant to Part IV of Act 498. The
insertion of this clause is necessary given the fact that Part IV of Act 498 has been
transferred into Part VI of the proposed Act.


-----

460 _Bill_

173. _Clauses 387 and 388 relate to the revocation of specific subsidiary legislation_
as specified. Such revocation is necessary as they have been incorporated into the
specific Schedules to the proposed act or may no longer be relevant with the
coming into effect of the proposed Act.

174. _Clauses 389 to 391 provide for the modifications to the construction of other_
written laws.

175. _Clause 392 provides that persons dealing in securities in relation to unit trust_
scheme that are members of a body approved by the Commission under the
repealed Act 280 shall for the purposes of clause 76 of the proposed Act be treated
as registered persons.

176. _Clause 393 provides for a transition period of one year to enable unlicensed_
unit trust management companies to be licensed under the proposed Act.

177. _Clause 394 relates to provisional provisions for corporate finance executives_
and research analysts.

_FINANCIAL IMPLICATIONS_

This Bill will not involve the Government in any extra financial expenditure.
